Name space for all Play\+Rho related names.

\Hypertarget{namespaceplayrho_a51e61fee8a0be399ed24773ebc3135f8}\label{namespaceplayrho_a51e61fee8a0be399ed24773ebc3135f8} 
\index{playrho@{playrho}!Fixed32@{Fixed32}}
\index{Fixed32@{Fixed32}!playrho@{playrho}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Fixed32}{Fixed32}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily using \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceplayrho_a51e61fee8a0be399ed24773ebc3135f8}{playrho\+::\+Fixed32}} = typedef \mbox{\hyperlink{classplayrho_1_1Fixed}{Fixed}}$<$std\+::int32\+\_\+t,9$>$}



32-\/bit fixed precision type. 

This is a 32-\/bit fixed precision type with a Q number-\/format of {\ttfamily Q23.\+9}.

\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
The available numeric fidelity of any 32-\/bit fixed point type is very limited. Using a 32-\/bit fixed point type for Real should only be considered for simulations where it\textquotesingle{}s been found to work and where the dynamics won\textquotesingle{}t be changing between runs.
\end{DoxyWarning}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
Maximum value (with 9 fraction bits) is approximately 4194303.\+99609375. 

Minimum value (with 9 fraction bits) is approximately 0.\+001953125.
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}

\Hypertarget{namespaceplayrho_a1fc125070a08100d083a1360f7167f87}\label{namespaceplayrho_a1fc125070a08100d083a1360f7167f87} 
\index{playrho@{playrho}!Real@{Real}}
\index{Real@{Real}!playrho@{playrho}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Real}{Real}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily using \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceplayrho_a1fc125070a08100d083a1360f7167f87}{playrho\+::\+Real}} = typedef float}



Real-\/number type. 

This is the number type underlying numerical calculations conceptually involving real-\/numbers. Ideally the implementation of this type doesn\textquotesingle{}t suffer from things like\+: catastrophic cancellation, catastrophic division, overflows, nor underflows.

\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
This can be implemented using any of the fundamental floating point types ( {\ttfamily float}, {\ttfamily double}, or {\ttfamily long double}). 

This can also be implemented using a {\ttfamily Literal\+Type} that has the necessary support\+: all common mathematical functions, support for infinity and NaN, and a specialization of the {\ttfamily std\+::numeric\+\_\+limits} class template for it. 

At present, the {\ttfamily Fixed32} and {\ttfamily Fixed64} aliases of the {\ttfamily \doxylink{classplayrho_1_1Fixed}{Fixed}} template type are provided as examples of qualifying literal types though the usability of these are limited and their use is discouraged.

Regarding division\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item While dividing 1 by a real, caching the result, and then doing multiplications with the result may well be faster (than repeatedly dividing), dividing 1 by the real can also result in an underflow situation that\textquotesingle{}s then compounded every time it\textquotesingle{}s multiplied with other values.
\item Meanwhile, dividing every time by a real isolates any underflows to the particular division where underflow occurs.
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
Using {\ttfamily Fixed32} is not advised as its numerical limitations are more likely to result in problems like overflows or underflows. 

The note regarding division applies even more so when using a fixed-\/point type (for {\ttfamily Real}).
\end{DoxyWarning}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\href{https://en.cppreference.com/w/cpp/language/types}{\texttt{ https\+://en.\+cppreference.\+com/w/cpp/language/types}} 

\href{https://en.cppreference.com/w/cpp/types/is_floating_point}{\texttt{ https\+://en.\+cppreference.\+com/w/cpp/types/is\+\_\+floating\+\_\+point}} 

\href{https://en.cppreference.com/w/cpp/named_req/LiteralType}{\texttt{ https\+://en.\+cppreference.\+com/w/cpp/named\+\_\+req/\+Literal\+Type}} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\doxylink{structplayrho_1_1Vector}{Vector} with 2 Real elements. 

\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
This data structure is two-\/times the size of the {\ttfamily Real} type (or 8 using Real of float). 
\end{DoxyNote}

\index{playrho@{playrho}!Alloc@{Alloc}}
\index{Alloc@{Alloc}!playrho@{playrho}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Alloc()}{Alloc()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} playrho\+::\+Alloc (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{std\+::size\+\_\+t}]{size }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Allocates memory. 

\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
One can change this function to use ones own memory allocator. Be sure to conform to this function\textquotesingle{}s interface\+: throw a {\ttfamily std\+::bad\+\_\+alloc} exception if unable to allocate non-\/zero sized memory and return a null pointer if the requested size is zero. This is done to ensure that the behavior is not implementation defined unlike {\ttfamily std\+::malloc}. 
\end{DoxyNote}

\begin{DoxyExceptions}{Exceptions}
{\em std\+::bad\+\_\+alloc} & If unable to allocate non-\/zero sized memory. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyExceptions}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Non-\/null pointer if size is not zero else {\ttfamily nullptr}. Pointer must be deallocated with {\ttfamily \doxylink{namespaceplayrho_a62c138018c11ab3c255b410f2dedd7d2}{Free(void\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*})}} or one of the {\ttfamily Realloc} functions. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\doxylink{namespaceplayrho_a62c138018c11ab3c255b410f2dedd7d2}{Free}, \doxylink{namespaceplayrho_adb651f620aefb4ee65ec0cc8c10b27b0}{Realloc}, \doxylink{namespaceplayrho_a0935e36656c30d9631f32184f4926e63}{Realloc\+Array}. 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\Hypertarget{namespaceplayrho_a1fb12b785f9e3a6b47cbb84b12162007}\label{namespaceplayrho_a1fb12b785f9e3a6b47cbb84b12162007}

Gets whether a given value is almost zero. 

An almost zero value is "{}subnormal"{}. Dividing by these values can lead to odd results like a divide by zero trap occurring. \begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
{\ttfamily true} if the given value is almost zero, {\ttfamily false} otherwise.

\index{playrho@{playrho}!MakeUnsigned@{MakeUnsigned}}
\index{MakeUnsigned@{MakeUnsigned}!playrho@{playrho}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{MakeUnsigned()}{MakeUnsigned()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T $>$ \\
constexpr std\+::enable\+\_\+if\+\_\+t$<$ std\+::is\+\_\+signed$<$ T $>$\+::value, std\+::make\+\_\+unsigned\+\_\+t$<$ T $>$ $>$ playrho\+::\+Make\+Unsigned (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const T \&}]{arg }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [constexpr]}, {\ttfamily [noexcept]}}



Makes the given {\bfseries{value}} into an {\bfseries{unsigned value}}. 

\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
If the given value is negative, this will result in an unsigned value which is the two\textquotesingle{}s complement modulo-\/wrapped value. 

This is different from {\ttfamily std\+::make\+\_\+unsigned} in that this changes the {\bfseries{value}} to the value in the type that\textquotesingle{}s the unsigned type equivalent of the input value. {\ttfamily std\+::make\+\_\+unsigned} merely provides the unsigned {\bfseries{type}} equivalent. 
\end{DoxyNote}

Multiplies an A-\/element vector by a A-\/by-\/B vector of vectors. 

\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
This algorithm favors column major ordering of the vector of vectors. 

This treats the left-\/hand-\/side argument as though it\textquotesingle{}s a 1-\/by-\/A vector of vectors. 
\end{DoxyNote}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em lhs} & Left-\/hand-\/side vector treated as if it were of type\+: {\ttfamily \doxylink{structplayrho_1_1Vector}{Vector}\texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}Vector$<$\+T1, A$>$, 1\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}}. \\
\hline
{\em rhs} & Right-\/hand-\/side vector of vectors. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
B-\/element vector product. 
\end{DoxyReturn}

Multiplies a B-\/by-\/A vector of vectors by an A-\/element vector. 

\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
This algorithm favors row major ordering of the vector of vectors. 

This treats the right-\/hand-\/side argument as though it\textquotesingle{}s an A-\/by-\/1 vector of vectors. 
\end{DoxyNote}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{operator\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}()}{operator*()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [7/8]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T1 , typename T2 , std\+::size\+\_\+t A, std\+::size\+\_\+t B, std\+::size\+\_\+t C, typename OT  = decltype(\+T1\{\} \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} T2\{\})$>$ \\
constexpr std\+::enable\+\_\+if\+\_\+t$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structplayrho_1_1IsMultipliable}{Is\+Multipliable}}$<$ T1, T2 $>$\+::value, \mbox{\hyperlink{structplayrho_1_1Vector}{Vector}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structplayrho_1_1Vector}{Vector}}$<$ OT, C $>$, A $>$ $>$ playrho\+::operator\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{structplayrho_1_1Vector}{Vector}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structplayrho_1_1Vector}{Vector}}$<$ T1, B $>$, A $>$ \&}]{lhs,  }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{structplayrho_1_1Vector}{Vector}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structplayrho_1_1Vector}{Vector}}$<$ T2, C $>$, B $>$ \&}]{rhs }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [constexpr]}, {\ttfamily [noexcept]}}



Calculates the matrix product of the two given vector of vectors (matrices). 

Multiplies an A-\/by-\/B vector of vectors by a B-\/by-\/C vector of vectors returning an A-\/by-\/C vector of vectors. \begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
From Wikipedia\+: \begin{quote}
Multiplication of two matrices is defined if and only if the number of columns of the left matrix is the same as the number of rows of the right matrix. \end{quote}


\doxylink{classMatrix}{Matrix} multiplication is not commutative. 

Algorithmically speaking, this implementation is called the "{}naive"{} algorithm. For small matrices, like 3-\/by-\/3 or smaller matrices, its complexity shouldn\textquotesingle{}t be an issue. The matrix dimensions are compile time constants anyway which can help compilers automatically identify loop unrolling and hardware level parallelism opportunities. 
\end{DoxyNote}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em lhs} & Left-\/hand-\/side matrix. \\
\hline
{\em rhs} & Right-\/hand-\/side matrix. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
A-\/by-\/C matrix product of the left-\/hand-\/side matrix and the right-\/hand-\/side matrix. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\href{https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matrix_multiplication}{\texttt{ https\+://en.\+wikipedia.\+org/wiki/\+Matrix\+\_\+multiplication}} 

\href{https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matrix_multiplication_algorithm}{\texttt{ https\+://en.\+wikipedia.\+org/wiki/\+Matrix\+\_\+multiplication\+\_\+algorithm}} 

\href{https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commutative_property}{\texttt{ https\+://en.\+wikipedia.\+org/wiki/\+Commutative\+\_\+property}} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\index{playrho@{playrho}!operator$<$@{operator$<$}}
\index{operator$<$@{operator$<$}!playrho@{playrho}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{operator$<$()}{operator<()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [3/4]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T $>$ \\
constexpr bool operator$<$ (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classplayrho_1_1Interval}{Interval}}$<$ T $>$ \&}]{lhs,  }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classplayrho_1_1Interval}{Interval}}$<$ T $>$ \&}]{rhs }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [constexpr]}, {\ttfamily [noexcept]}}



Less-\/than operator. 

\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
Provides a "{}strict weak ordering"{} relation. 

This is a lexicographical comparison. 

Obeys the {\ttfamily Less\+Than\+Comparable} named requirement\+: {\ttfamily for all a, !(a \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<} a); if (a \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<} b) then !(b \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<} a); if (a \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<} b) and (b \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<} c) then (a \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<} c); with equiv = !(a \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<} b) \&\& !(b \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<} a), if equiv(a, b) and equiv(b, c), then equiv(a, c).}
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\href{https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weak_ordering\#Strict_weak_orderings}{\texttt{ https\+://en.\+wikipedia.\+org/wiki/\+Weak\+\_\+ordering\#\+Strict\+\_\+weak\+\_\+orderings}} 

\href{https://en.cppreference.com/w/cpp/named_req/LessThanComparable}{\texttt{ https\+://en.\+cppreference.\+com/w/cpp/named\+\_\+req/\+Less\+Than\+Comparable}} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\index{playrho@{playrho}!Realloc@{Realloc}}
\index{Realloc@{Realloc}!playrho@{playrho}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Realloc()}{Realloc()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} playrho\+::\+Realloc (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{void \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{ptr,  }\item[{std\+::size\+\_\+t}]{size }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Reallocates memory. 

\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
One can change this function to use ones own memory allocator. Be sure to conform to this function\textquotesingle{}s interface\+: throw a {\ttfamily std\+::bad\+\_\+alloc} exception if unable to allocate non-\/zero sized memory, return a null pointer if the requested size is zero, and free old memory if the new size is zero. This is done to ensure that the behavior is not implementation defined unlike {\ttfamily std\+::realloc}. 

If the new size for memory is zero, then the old memory is freed. 
\end{DoxyNote}

\begin{DoxyExceptions}{Exceptions}
{\em std\+::bad\+\_\+alloc} & If unable to reallocate non-\/zero sized memory. Pointer must be deallocated with {\ttfamily \doxylink{namespaceplayrho_a62c138018c11ab3c255b410f2dedd7d2}{Free(void\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*})}} or one of the {\ttfamily Realloc} functions. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyExceptions}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Non-\/null pointer if size is not zero else {\ttfamily nullptr}. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\doxylink{namespaceplayrho_a516a3bbb73371cdc53f348b67f43bb1f}{Alloc}, \doxylink{namespaceplayrho_a62c138018c11ab3c255b410f2dedd7d2}{Free}. 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\Hypertarget{namespaceplayrho_a0935e36656c30d9631f32184f4926e63}\label{namespaceplayrho_a0935e36656c30d9631f32184f4926e63}

Default linear sleep tolerance.

A body cannot sleep if the magnitude of its linear velocity is above this amount. \Hypertarget{namespaceplayrho_ad91e53ba44755653e34147d39695a0a1}\label{namespaceplayrho_ad91e53ba44755653e34147d39695a0a1}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DefaultLinearSlop}{DefaultLinearSlop}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily constexpr auto playrho\+::\+Default\+Linear\+Slop = \mbox{\hyperlink{structplayrho_1_1detail_1_1Defaults}{detail\+::\+Defaults}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceplayrho_a1fc125070a08100d083a1360f7167f87}{Real}}$>$\+::\+Get\+Linear\+Slop()\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [constexpr]}}



Default linear slop. 

Length used as a collision and constraint tolerance. Usually chosen to be numerically significant, but visually insignificant. Lower or raise to decrease or increase respectively the minimum of space between bodies at rest. \begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
Smaller values relative to sizes of bodies increases the time it takes for bodies to come to rest. 
\end{DoxyNote}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{DefaultMaxSubSteps}{DefaultMaxSubSteps}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily constexpr auto playrho\+::\+Default\+Max\+Sub\+Steps = std\+::uint8\+\_\+t\{8\}\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [constexpr]}}

Default maximum number of sub steps.

This is the default maximum number of sub-\/steps per contact in continuous physics simulation. In other words, this is the default maximum number of times in a world step that a contact will have continuous collision resolution done for it. \begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
Used in the TOI phase of step processing. 
\end{DoxyNote}

Maximum number of contacts in a world (2147319811). 

Uses the formula for the maximum number of edges in an unidirectional graph of {\ttfamily Max\+Bodies} nodes. This occurs when every possible body is connected to every other body. \Hypertarget{namespaceplayrho_af36288c4602f14acd96242145a546980}\label{namespaceplayrho_af36288c4602f14acd96242145a546980}

\Hypertarget{namespaceplayrho_a3fe0bdbb0ea9c449b7504f7c75840993}\label{namespaceplayrho_a3fe0bdbb0ea9c449b7504f7c75840993} 
\index{playrho@{playrho}!Pi@{Pi}}
\index{Pi@{Pi}!playrho@{playrho}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Pi}{Pi}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily constexpr auto playrho\+::\+Pi = \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceplayrho_a1fc125070a08100d083a1360f7167f87}{Real}}(3.\+14159265358979323846264338327950288)\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [constexpr]}}



Pi. 

An "{}irrational number"{} that\textquotesingle{}s defined as the ratio of a circle\textquotesingle{}s circumference to its diameter.

\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
While the include file definition of M\+\_\+\+PI may be a POSIX compliance requirement and initially attractive to use, it\textquotesingle{}s apparently not a C++ standards requirement and casually including it pollutes the name space of all code that uses this library. Whatever the case, MSVC 2017 doesn\textquotesingle{}t make it part of the {\ttfamily cmath} include without enabling {\ttfamily \+\_\+\+USE\+\_\+\+MATH\+\_\+\+DEFINES}. So rather than add yet more C preprocessor macros to all sources that this library may be compiled with, it\textquotesingle{}s simply hard-\/coded in here instead using a C++ mechanism that also keeps it with the enclosing name space. 

Any narrowing is intentional.
\end{DoxyNote}

\href{https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pi}{\texttt{ https\+://en.\+wikipedia.\+org/wiki/\+Pi}} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
